    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<span id="freeTextContainer6944044470580211015">Lo Blacklock, a journalist who writes for a travel magazine, has just been given the assignment of a lifetime: a week on a luxury cruise with only a handful of cabins. The sky is clear, the waters calm, and the veneered, select guests jovial as the exclusive cruise ship, the Aurora, begins her voyage in the picturesque North Sea. At first, Lo's stay is nothing but pleasant</span>
  <span id="freeText6944044470580211015" style="display:none">Lo Blacklock, a journalist who writes for a travel magazine, has just been given the assignment of a lifetime: a week on a luxury cruise with only a handful of cabins. The sky is clear, the waters calm, and the veneered, select guests jovial as the exclusive cruise ship, the Aurora, begins her voyage in the picturesque North Sea. At first, Lo's stay is nothing but pleasant: the cabins are plush, the dinner parties are sparkling, and the guests are elegant. But as the week wears on, frigid winds whip the deck, gray skies fall, and Lo witnesses what she can only describe as a dark and terrifying nightmare: a woman being thrown overboard. The problem? All passengers remain accounted for and so, the ship sails on as if nothing has happened, despite Lo's desperate attempts to convey that something (or someone) has gone terribly, terribly wrong.</span>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});
        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Is it just me or did anyone else find the main character in this book totally unlikable? It seems to me she is rude to almost everyone in the book, in<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Is it just me or did anyone else find the main character in this book totally unlikable? It seems to me she is rude to almost everyone in the book, including the man who loves her-who happens to be the only likable character in the whole book. I just have a hard time caring about a book when the main character is rude and uncaring about everyone but herself. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/5052581-joe-g"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1473969048i/5052581._UX100_CR0,53,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/5052581-joe-g">Joe G</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    So, a couple of things...Richard was definitely killed by Carrie b/c Lo saw the news clip of his death on TV. Obviously the gun Lo saw in the drawer w<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    So, a couple of things...Richard was definitely killed by Carrie b/c Lo saw the news clip of his death on TV. Obviously the gun Lo saw in the drawer was the weapon. I also believe that Ann was alive when she was tossed overboard. Carrie thought that as well as she told Lo that. The press release said Ann's death was due to drowning not a trauma, so, she was alive when tossed to sea. Carrie kills Richard and wires the money (obviously from Ann's fortune). What makes the ending a bit of a stretch is 1. Lo had all of Anns ID--passport etc. 2. How did Carrie get the details to access Anns fortune? 3. How did she get the details of Lo's bank account to wire the money to her? Those are loose ends that I wish were taken care of by the author. <a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>
</div>
</span>

<div id="review_1574705478" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1574705478" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31923026-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1533734143p2/31923026.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1574705478?book_show_action=true">Mar 09, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/31923026-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31923026-laura?shelf=crime-mystery-thriller">crime-mystery-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31923026-laura?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1574705478" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11786604144294064801">Meh. I enjoyed Ruth Ware's debut a lot more than this one. I found I was expected to suspend my disbelief even more in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28187230.The_Woman_in_Cabin_10' title='The Woman in Cabin 10 by Ruth Ware' rel='nofollow noopener'> The Woman in Cabin 10</a> and I wasn't having any of it. It also felt like a not as good carbon copy of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22557272.The_Girl_on_the_Train' title='The Girl on the Train by Paula Hawkins' rel='nofollow noopener'> The Girl on the Train</a>. Usually even with all the similarities of thrillers these days, I can find enough originality in the story to feel the author didn't *try* to follow the same formula. That didn't exactly happen here. It felt like the author just replaced a few facts with s</span>
  <span id="freeText11786604144294064801" style="display:none">Meh. I enjoyed Ruth Ware's debut a lot more than this one. I found I was expected to suspend my disbelief even more in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28187230.The_Woman_in_Cabin_10" title="The Woman in Cabin 10 by Ruth Ware" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Woman in Cabin 10</a> and I wasn't having any of it. It also felt like a not as good carbon copy of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22557272.The_Girl_on_the_Train" title="The Girl on the Train by Paula Hawkins" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Girl on the Train</a>. Usually even with all the similarities of thrillers these days, I can find enough originality in the story to feel the author didn't *try* to follow the same formula. That didn't exactly happen here. It felt like the author just replaced a few facts with similar enough things..changed the train into a luxury cruise liner. Changed a few details here and there. And boom...here's a new book. I guess I'll delve into the plot a tiny bit to get my point across while still avoiding spoilers.<br /><br />Laura Blacklock (she goes by Lo) suffers from extreme anxiety to the point of needing medicine to keep it under control. When a break-in occurs in her apartment with her present, it brings her fear and anxiety to a whole new high. Lo's sleep is suffering a great deal. She got in a huge fight with her boyfriend. But she still has to go on this week long luxury cruise assignment for work since her boss is on maternity leave. This could be her way of finally getting that promotion if Lo can just keep it together enough to network among important people and help put their small travel magazine, <i>Velocity</i>, on the map.<br /><br />The <i>Aurora</i> is a brand new super-luxury cruise liner that will travel around the Norwegian fjords for it's maiden voyage. It's rather small with only 10 cabins, a maximum of 20 passengers, and a handpicked staff on board. Lo is roomed in cabin 9. It isn't far into the trip when Lo is woken by a scream from the cabin next door followed by a loud splash. She goes out onto the veranda to see blood on the neighboring balcony. She calls security to report what happened, but there's nothing in cabin 10. The guest who was supposed to be in that room didn't make the cruise. Which is odd because Lo swears she borrowed mascara from a girl in cabin 10 before dinner. There aren't any passengers missing, staff unaccounted for, nothing amiss other than Lo's report of what she witnessed. Is her anxiety-ridden mind mixed with the lack of sleep and abundance of alcohol playing tricks on her? Lo insists something happened. Nobody believes her. <br /><br />So I felt like we took Lo and made her unlikable and unreliable in the same way that was done in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22557272.The_Girl_on_the_Train" title="The Girl on the Train by Paula Hawkins" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Girl on the Train</a>. Replace the alcoholism with intense anxiety giving others reason to question her reliability as a witness. It's another protagonist witnesses murder and no one believes her story. Add in the means of transportation...boat in place of train. It feels really similar. The twist isn't the same, though. But that's where my next problem resides. Was that even really much of a twist?! Yeah..the first part of it was good, but when it came to the actual end..I was left thinking it was unbelievably dumb because it was obvious. And I don't understand for the life of me how Lo didn't put that together. Is she stupid? Well maybe because a lot of what she did through the book did not make sense. I couldn't see the logic in her head even with all that she had going on.<br /><br />Plus her ex-boyfriend happens to be one of the other reporters on board adding a dose of drama. Because who else would Lo be able to get to believe her if anyone? I hated the way these two interacted. It made Lo appear even more weak. I couldn't stand it. This was probably on purpose no matter how aggravating it made Lo. It's annoying because the set up for the story was so great - a possible murder on a cruise ship in the middle of the ocean. It was a locked-room mystery a la <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/123715.Agatha_Christie" title="Agatha Christie" rel="nofollow noopener"> Agatha Christie</a>, who might have done this better. This is something I've noticed in both <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/9013543.Ruth_Ware" title="Ruth Ware" rel="nofollow noopener"> Ruth Ware</a>'s books - her inspirations from the classic author. I do hope to see more of this. I only wish this one had worked better. It was too similar to The Girl on the Train and had too many implausible moments for me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11786604144294064801" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2372754979" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2372754979" />
    <a title="Miranda Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads"><img alt="Miranda Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592243041p2/71848701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2372754979?book_show_action=true">Apr 25, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miranda Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miranda Reads" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads">Miranda Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2372754979" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17989790107274534555">3.5 stars<blockquote>
  <i>"There’s a reason why we keep thoughts inside our heads for the most part—they’re not safe to be let out in public."</i>
</blockquote> Laura "Lo" Blacklock just won the career lottery - her pregnant boss can no longer attend the Aurora cruise. Instead, her boss sends Lo as the magazine's representative to<b> the maiden voyage.</b> <blockquote>
  <i>“For a travel journalist I’m worryingly bad at geography.” </i>
</blockquote><b>The ship is full </b>of rich socialites, intrepid reporters and world-renowned rich folks - the perfect people to <b>wine &</b></span>
  <span id="freeText17989790107274534555" style="display:none">3.5 stars<blockquote>
  <i>"There’s a reason why we keep thoughts inside our heads for the most part—they’re not safe to be let out in public."</i>
</blockquote> Laura "Lo" Blacklock just won the career lottery - her pregnant boss can no longer attend the Aurora cruise. Instead, her boss sends Lo as the magazine's representative to<b> the maiden voyage.</b> <blockquote>
  <i>“For a travel journalist I’m worryingly bad at geography.” </i>
</blockquote><b>The ship is full </b>of rich socialites, intrepid reporters and world-renowned rich folks - the perfect people to <b>wine &amp; dine</b>. Lo can feel it in her bones -<i>
  <b> this is her chance.</b>
</i> Right before she sets off - her apartment is broken into, and she feels fear like she's never felt it before.<br /><br />The very first night, she borrows mascara from<b> the woman in cabin 10</b> (hey-o it's the title!). Later that night, Lo hears a splash outside and sees what looks like a <b>body sinking beneath the waves.</b><br /><br />Only, when <b>she raises the alarm</b>...everyone on the ship is accounted for. What's more, given Lo's shakey use of medication, and her general lack of evidence, fewer and fewer people believe her. Even the mascara -<b> her one shred of proof </b>- goes missing. <blockquote>
  <i>“I know what it's like. Don't you see? I know what she must have felt like, when someone came for her in the middle of the night. That's why I have to find out who did this to her.” </i>
</blockquote>As frustrations (and her own desperation) mounts, Lo is faced with the<b> single most defining decision in her life</b> - was there ever a girl in the cabin or could it have been all in her head? <br /><br />This one was certainly engaging and I think the author did a fairly good job with the atmosphere and the setting. <br /><br />As Lo became more and more panicked, I felt adrenaline jumping. <br /><br />However, there were certainly moments where the pacing felt really...off... where things would slow, slow, slowww down for no apparent reason. Really took me out of the book. <br /><br />This one had a similar feel to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22557272.The_Girl_on_the_Train" title="The Girl on the Train by Paula Hawkins" rel="nofollow noopener">The Girl on the Train</a> - though this one had a <b>main character with an actual backbone.</b> (Well, sort of. Lo did get a bit weepy and annoying about 2/3 of the way through).<br /><br />Overall, an entertaining read - and I didn't see the ending coming.<br /><br /><b>Audiobook Comments</b><br />Extremely well-read by Imogen Church. This was set in England/Norway and the accents sounded rather good (to my untrained ear). Though...the reader's Brooklyn accent (for Lo's boyfriend) really could've used some work. It wasn't enough to ruin the audiobook, but it was certainly something I noticed...<br /><br /><a href="http://bit.ly/33ii2CT" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | Snapchat @miranda.reads <br /><br />Happy Reading!</span>

<div id="review_1580338619" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1580338619" />
    <a title="Chelsea Humphrey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47207032-chelsea-humphrey"><img alt="Chelsea Humphrey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585613513p2/47207032.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1580338619?book_show_action=true">Mar 15, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea Humphrey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea Humphrey" href="/user/show/47207032-chelsea-humphrey">Chelsea Humphrey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781501132940" href="/book/show/28188211-the-woman-in-cabin-10">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47207032-chelsea-humphrey?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1580338619&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1580338619" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5697969897926349609">Thank you Netgalley for my copy in exchange for a fair and honest review.<br/><br/>I should start by saying I ended up not reading the author's first book, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23346377.In_a_Dark__Dark_Wood' title='In a Dark, Dark Wood by Ruth Ware' rel='nofollow noopener'>In a Dark, Dark Wood</a>, because someone I know spoiled the whole "big twist" for me. I also should say I wasn't very disappointed as I wouldn't have enjoyed spending all the time invested reading it for another <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19288043.Gone_Girl' title='Gone Girl by Gillian Flynn' rel='nofollow noopener'>Gone Girl</a> wannabe. I'm getting a little tired of everyone wanting to write the next big hit in the genre, but writing THE EXACT same story with d</span>
  <span id="freeText5697969897926349609" style="display:none">Thank you Netgalley for my copy in exchange for a fair and honest review.<br /><br />I should start by saying I ended up not reading the author's first book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23346377.In_a_Dark__Dark_Wood" title="In a Dark, Dark Wood by Ruth Ware" rel="nofollow noopener">In a Dark, Dark Wood</a>, because someone I know spoiled the whole "big twist" for me. I also should say I wasn't very disappointed as I wouldn't have enjoyed spending all the time invested reading it for another <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19288043.Gone_Girl" title="Gone Girl by Gillian Flynn" rel="nofollow noopener">Gone Girl</a> wannabe. I'm getting a little tired of everyone wanting to write the next big hit in the genre, but writing THE EXACT same story with differently named characters. <br /><br />I'll also say that, while comparing the plots of her two books, this one was loads improved and I was interested to see what she wrote next, as I felt it would be more a show of her own work instead of trying to be the next big thing. You can read the plot for this one on the book page, but basically, Lo is a journalist who has the opportunity to cover a story aboard a swanky new cruise ship where things start to go awry.<br /><br />Because so few people have read this so far, I'm not going to hash out every problem I had with this book, but I'll give some very vague generalizations as to not ruin the experience for someone else. I had big problems with the very beginning and the last 20% of this book. The middle 60% was honestly spot on, and if the entire book had been written with that sense of excellency it would have been a 5 star read.<br /><br />THINGS I LIKED:<br />Another reviewer named Denise brought this up first, but I liked how she described the format of this book reading like a classic <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/123715.Agatha_Christie" title="Agatha Christie" rel="nofollow noopener">Agatha Christie</a> novel. Group of people confined in a small area surrounding a murder. This is always a plus for me. I fangirl over any and all things reminiscent of Christie. <br /><br />The pacing, after the first 25% was great! The suspense built, layer upon layer, until you just wanted to devour the rest to find out "whodunnit". Unfortunately, you do find out who the culprit is a little earlier than expected, with a few minor twists nearing the end.<br /><br />There was one big twist I 100% did not see coming. I always like being taken off my game so this was a positive for me; however, I can already see many people having a problem with not only this twist, but the whole dang book because everything was very unrealistic.<br /><br />THINGS I DISLIKED:<br />Lo Blacklock. Dear God, I loathed this woman. I've never had to follow the story of such a peculiar, whiny, uncomfortable woman in all my reading. She did seem to find a backbone toward the end which I did appreciate. I'm just not sure how to pity a woman who is defined by passages like this (paraphrasing by me): <br />"I don't want to have sex with you Ben"-Lo<br />*Ben grabs Lo's breast in attempt to have sex with her anyway*<br />*Lo knees Ben in crotch*<br />SCENE<br />Immediately following, Lo is crying in her room with Ben's arm around her and he is trying to make her feel less guilty for her kneeing him in the crotch. This, proceeded by the mascara incident (which I know was an important scene in the book), just grated on me. <br /><br />So many random incidents happen in this book without being tied together or having any explanation. I think she threw certain plot points in to give us a better overall understanding of Lo and her bizarre actions, but it just didn't work for me. I honestly am sitting here and am not entirely sure I even know how this book ended. <br /><br />If you enjoyed her first book, you will very likely enjoy this one as well. I can't say I didn't enjoy this one, as it was a quick, compelling read, but I did expect much more from it. This felt jumbled, confusing, and like a debut that you expect to be a little rough. There is definitely talent here; I'm hoping book 3 will show stronger growth in the author's writing, but I still think I would recommend to those who are looking for an easy, quick read to capture their attention. And I hope you all don't hate me for not loving this book as much as you probably will. :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="5697969897926349609" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7035982926737554599">My initial reaction upon finishing <i>The Woman in Cabin 10</i> can best be summed up as follows:<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471188933ra/20010265.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I read it. I'm not mad about it. <br/><br/>It was good, though not a new favorite; final thought:<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1441014204ra/16052343.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Meh.<br/><br/>((<i>all the shrugs</i>))<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1440106208ra/15930293.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Admittedly, there is something very addictive about Ware's writing. <br/><br/>For me, the second half of this novel saved it from a lower rating.   <span id="freeText7035982926737554599" style="display:none">My initial reaction upon finishing <i>The Woman in Cabin 10</i> can best be summed up as follows:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471188933ra/20010265.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I read it. I'm not mad about it. <br><br>It was good, though not a new favorite; final thought:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1441014204ra/16052343.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Meh.<br><br>((<i>all the shrugs</i>))<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1440106208ra/15930293.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Admittedly, there is something very addictive about Ware's writing. <br><br>For me, the second half of this novel saved it from a lower rating. I wasn't really invested in the story at all until the reveal. <br><br>The reveal itself, as well as the events leading up to the final conclusion, were more compelling than the build-up to the reveal. Because of this, I would say this one felt uneven.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1549482107ra/27025243.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>During the build-up, I had quite a few moments of frustration with our protagonist. Thinking, <i>Who cares?! God, Lo, mind your business. Please, quit whining!</i><br><br>Then the reveal happened and I was like, <i>hold up now, that's kind of interesting...</i>. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1549482107ra/27025242.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Yeah, so keeping it short and sweet, those are my thoughts. <br><br>Q: Would I classify this as one of the best mystery/thrillers I have ever read? <br>A: No. <br><br>Q: Will I read another Ruth Ware book? <br>A: Definitely. <br><br>I'm accepting no further questions at this time. Take from that what you will.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1537027808ra/26306903.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div id="review_1734826222" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1734826222" />
    <a title="Will M." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20408288-will-m"><img alt="Will M." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452951660p2/20408288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1734826222?book_show_action=true">Aug 21, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Will M." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Will M." href="/user/show/20408288-will-m">Will M.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=crime-mystery-thriller">crime-mystery-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1734826222" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17158816635324224188">The Woman in Cabin 10 promised an intense read, but all I felt after reading this was intense anger. Anger because I expected so much more than what the author promised. The premise is typical of a thriller novel, it depicts a rollercoaster ride. This novel unfortunately is a huge disappointment for me. So much time wasted.<br/><br/>I listened to this book because I had other books I was already reading, and I need to listen to a book while driving. The narrator didn't have the most pleasing voice, but sh</span>
  <span id="freeText17158816635324224188" style="display:none">The Woman in Cabin 10 promised an intense read, but all I felt after reading this was intense anger. Anger because I expected so much more than what the author promised. The premise is typical of a thriller novel, it depicts a rollercoaster ride. This novel unfortunately is a huge disappointment for me. So much time wasted.<br /><br />I listened to this book because I had other books I was already reading, and I need to listen to a book while driving. The narrator didn't have the most pleasing voice, but she still did a good job. I believe that the character the author created, Lo, is the problem. She's a rude, conceited, and honestly a bit stupid. I hate thrillers with a good plot but has terrible characters. This novel has terrible characters and a mediocre plot. <br /><br />It all started with Lo and a certain event in her flat. That event made her paranoid and affected most of what happens next in the novel. When she finally got aboard The Aurora, I thought that it should get really good from here, but right from the start of her being onboard, it starts to get really dull and annoying. I didn't like her approach to people, even if the justification is because of what happened to her before, it's a bit unlikely that anyone is that rude. If I were to meet her in person, I would most likely hate her just from the introduction. The climax of the novel shouldn't even be considered as a real climax, because there is none. It's all rambling and talking to the crew. The mystery started to seem really boring because of all her rambling and complaining about everything. <br /><br />The most annoying part of the novel is the disgusting ending and revelation of the secret. That's it? I wasted 9 hours of my life listening to this piece of crap? I've read way better thrillers with cliches plot than this. This is probably the most overhyped book I've read in my life. I'm glad I didn't buy a physical copy because I might give it away to a person that I hate. I firmly believe that it wouldn't have made a difference if I read this, because I would be equally annoyed with the outcome, and the main character.<br /><br />After days of contemplating ,I can't give this more than 1 star. Whenever I remember this novel, there's no positive feeling or emotion felt toward it. If only I could forget about novels, this would be a good use of that ability. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17158816635324224188" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2209658639" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2209658639" />
    <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines"><img alt="Elle (ellexamines)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582250895p2/52545435.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2209658639?book_show_action=true">Jan 26, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elle (ellexamines)" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines">Elle (ellexamines)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-read2018">z-read2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=zzzzz-did-not-finish">zzzzz-did-not-finish</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=y-out2016">y-out2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-coverporn">z-coverporn</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=x-audiobook">x-audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=1-star">1-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2209658639" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8826388236371082402">I just realized I don't hate myself and therefore will not be completing this. if you look up the word mediocre in the dictionary it’s just a photo of this book. maybe a photo of the opening page because the cover is the only thing about this that isn’t shit<br/><br/>Listen, this is just about the most generic thriller ever written. Let’s talk about all the shitty ass ways this book copies <i>The Girl on the Train</i>, a 2015 novel that I have an immense distaste for. They have the <i>exact same plot.</i> Lead observes</span>
  <span id="freeText8826388236371082402" style="display:none">I just realized I don't hate myself and therefore will not be completing this. if you look up the word mediocre in the dictionary it’s just a photo of this book. maybe a photo of the opening page because the cover is the only thing about this that isn’t shit<br /><br />Listen, this is just about the most generic thriller ever written. Let’s talk about all the shitty ass ways this book copies <i>The Girl on the Train</i>, a 2015 novel that I have an immense distaste for. They have the <i>exact same plot.</i> Lead observes something. But no one will believe her because she is <i>Un Re Li Able.</i> You can read literally any one of these novels and there’s an unreliable narrator. Why is she unreliable? Some unspecific mental condition that will play into her character development absolutely zero! Or better yet, alcoholism! <br /><br /><b>It is 2018. The Girl on the Train was a shitty book. Stop copying it.</b><br /><br />And listen, okay, I am fine with unreliable narrators. But in books like these we know from the <i>beginning</i> that they’re unreliable and that they might be hallucinating it all. Ooooooooooooooooh. You know what else we know? <b>That no author is going to end the book with “yup, they hallucinated that all.”</b> Because then how can you market it to work-tired middle-aged readers to bring on their Bahamas trip? Although I’m sure a vaguely boring sixty year old scholar somewhere could work out a marketing pitch about how an ending with no reveal simply demonstrates the pointlessness of existing. They would be wrong. Nothing could possibly be as pointless as this book. <br /><br />Also, you know, <b>complex characters do need to have some vague veneer of consistency</b>. For example, let’s say your lead character looooooooves her boyfriend. She wants to solve all the issues in their relationship and be with him forever. So what does she do? Something nice? Of course not, because that would be logical! She gets in a fight with him and proceeds to ignore all his emails for days. Yeah.<br /><br />And you know what? You get a bonus fucking round for the cringiest thing that happened in this book. The main character’s ex-boyfriend touches her boobs without any consent or even hint she’s into him. She knees him in the groin for touching her boob. Great, right? No, because Ruth Ware then promptly ruins the iconicness of the moment by having her protagonist apologize for it and say it was her fault. <b>He touched her on the boob without asking. He absolutely deserved to be kneed in the balls.</b> <br /><br />this book can actually go jump in the ocean. just like that woman who still has not been thrown in the ocean despite me being THIRTY ONE FUCKING PERCENT IN and it being in the damn BLURB. I'm going to bed.<br /><br /><a href="https://thebookishactress.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/52545435" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodreads</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/jespergayhey" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://www.youtube.com/channel/UCVIY_GxZIuclzsIw9CLSe3g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="8826388236371082402" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1580358613?book_show_action=true">Mar 15, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9472704-linda?shelf=psychological-thriller">psychological-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9472704-linda?shelf=mystery-thrillers">mystery-thrillers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9472704-linda?shelf=net-galley">net-galley</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1580358613" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6984531400498734544">I received a copy of The Woman in Cabin 10 from NetGalley for an honest review. Thank you to NetGalley, Gallery Scout Press, and Ruth Ware for the opportunity. This book will be published in July, 2016.<br/><br/>You know the feeling.....poised for sound and vigilant for any hint of the slightest evidence of movement. You are alone. At least that is what your mind tells you.<br/><br/>Lo Blacklock has barely an eye open after a night of some serious throwing 'em back drinking. But there are sounds coming from the out</span>
  <span id="freeText6984531400498734544" style="display:none">I received a copy of The Woman in Cabin 10 from NetGalley for an honest review. Thank you to NetGalley, Gallery Scout Press, and Ruth Ware for the opportunity. This book will be published in July, 2016.<br /><br />You know the feeling.....poised for sound and vigilant for any hint of the slightest evidence of movement. You are alone. At least that is what your mind tells you.<br /><br />Lo Blacklock has barely an eye open after a night of some serious throwing 'em back drinking. But there are sounds coming from the outer periphery of her tiny basement apartment. And why is the door closed? A turn of the doorknob reveals a man completely encased in a cocoon of black clothing and wearing latex gloves. Shock finds Lo instantly and she is completely immobile. The door slams and Lo is locked inside.<br /><br />Later, Lo is able to break out of her bedroom prison. But the break-in leaves Lo shattered and filled with fear. It has a downward affect on her relationship with her boyfriend as well. Lo gladly accepts an assignment from the travel magazine that she works for in order to flee from this nightmare. She boards the cruise liner, Aurora Borealis, on its maiden voyage. No harm can ever come to her way out in the distant waters. She finally embraces a haven that she believes to be safe. But is she really?<br /><br />And here comes an injection of "gaslighting" at its finest. Lo experiences the freight train collision of witnessing a body being tossed overboard. She runs next door to Cabin 10 to alert the woman who had just loaned her a mascara earlier in the evening. No one is there and no passenger has been booked for that cabin. In fact, the passenger/crew list is intact. No one, but no one, is left unaccounted for. Have too many rounds of gin and tonic left Lo's brain pickled and off kilter?<br /><br />The tension mounts as Lo clings to what she believes and feels actually happened. But there are no takers for the story that is ripping her to shreds inside. Self-doubt wants to take permanent residence inside her already fragile mind taunt with high-pitched anxiety.<br /><br />Ruth Ware provides an easy, quick writing style. The dialogue is crisp and not bogged down with endless soliloquy. The build-up is relentless. As the reader, you take pity on Lo and don't want to leave her adrift here. So you keep turning pages.....<br /><br />Now the conclusion may or may not fit the bill for you. We each bring our own experiential backgrounds to the act of reading. But I will say this, I'm glad to have taken that eerie cruise with Lo. It will not leave you adrift with wonder. It all plays out in those deep, deep waters.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6984531400498734544" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1759704842?book_show_action=true">Jan 23, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Norma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Norma" href="/user/show/41400192-norma">Norma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1759704842" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4055436318379282536">Well that was a much better read for me than the author's first book, IN A DARK, DARK WOOD as it was slow-moving for me and just didn't maintain my interest. This one though was fast-paced and had me entertained and engaged right from the very first chapter.<br/><br/>THE WOMAN IN CABIN 10 by RUTH WARE was a chilling and suspenseful thriller with the perfect setting for a mystery on a small luxurious cruise liner with only 10 cabins set to sail from London to Norway. I was really intrigued with the setting</span>
  <span id="freeText4055436318379282536" style="display:none">Well that was a much better read for me than the author's first book, IN A DARK, DARK WOOD as it was slow-moving for me and just didn't maintain my interest. This one though was fast-paced and had me entertained and engaged right from the very first chapter.<br /><br />THE WOMAN IN CABIN 10 by RUTH WARE was a chilling and suspenseful thriller with the perfect setting for a mystery on a small luxurious cruise liner with only 10 cabins set to sail from London to Norway. I was really intrigued with the setting and plot of this novel as I have always wanted to take a vacation on a Luxury Cruise Liner. <br /><br />I fell in love with THE COVER of this book when I first seen it and have been obsessed with reading it ever since, that is the main reason that I chose this book to read. Awesome embossed cover of water spots on a porthole window with the ocean waves in the background!<br /><br />THE WOMAN IN CABIN 10 isn't all that creative of a TITLE but is fitting as there is a mystery that develops as we follow along the voyage of the Aurora about who the woman in Cabin 10 is that Laura (Lo) Blacklock seen and believes to have been murdered. Her sanity is questioned here as Cabin 10 was unoccupied but she is determined to prove that someone was indeed in Cabin 10 and murdered.<br /><br />This novel was filled with a few CHARACTERS and I had a little bit of problem at times keeping track of who the secondary ones were, but it didn't really disrupt me from the storyline though. RUTH WARE delivers an atmospheric and suspenseful story here with a few good twists that had me questioning and guessing what actually happened and who was involved. Although there were a few things that happened in this book that I felt were never answered or was missing from the plot.<br /><br />The ENDING was intense, exciting, and very satisfying with a surprising twist for another enjoyable read.<br /><br />To sum it all up it was an entertaining, enjoyable, suspenseful, fast-paced, quick and easy read with a twist ending. Would recommend!!<br /><br />Review can also be found on Two Sisters Lost in a Coulee Reading:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://travelingsistersbookreviews.com/">https://travelingsistersbookreviews.com/</a></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3386415733374326326">My reviews can also be seen at: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://deesradreadsandreviews.wordpress.com/'>https://deesradreadsandreviews.wordpr...</a><br/><br/>3.5 stars<br/><br/>This is my first book by Ruth Ware. I have always wanted to take a luxury cruise and so the plot of this book intrigued me.<br/><br/>I was actually going to read Dark Dark Wood prior to reading this novel. However, since I won a copy of this book from a Goodreads Giveaway, so I figured I could always go back and read Dark Dark Wood some other time. <br/><br/>Journalist, Laura (Lo) Blacklock is a writer for a travel magazine. Lo suffers</span>
  <span id="freeText3386415733374326326" style="display:none">My reviews can also be seen at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://deesradreadsandreviews.wordpress.com/">https://deesradreadsandreviews.wordpr...</a><br /><br />3.5 stars<br /><br />This is my first book by Ruth Ware. I have always wanted to take a luxury cruise and so the plot of this book intrigued me.<br /><br />I was actually going to read Dark Dark Wood prior to reading this novel. However, since I won a copy of this book from a Goodreads Giveaway, so I figured I could always go back and read Dark Dark Wood some other time. <br /><br />Journalist, Laura (Lo) Blacklock is a writer for a travel magazine. Lo suffers from anxiety and after a terrifying home invasion she doesn't feel safe anywhere anymore. Maybe her new work assignment will help. It is a free week-long trip on a luxury cruise. This assignment could also help with the promotion she's been wanting.<br /><br />The Aurora is a beautiful brand new boat. Luxurious but small and intimate with only ten cabins. <br /><br />But the assignment of a lifetime soon turns into a nightmare when Lo is positive she sees a woman from the cabin next door thrown off the boat. But that can't have happened as all passengers on the boat are accounted for....<br /><br />Lo is insistent and knows that she didn't imagine the woman she spoke to, the woman even gave her a tube of mascara. So where is she now? Where is the woman from cabin 10?<br /><br />No one seems to take her concerns seriously.<br /><br />Did she have too much to drink? Is she losing her mind?<br /><br />I did have a bit of trouble getting into the book at first. I'm not entirely sure why but I found my mind wandering. However, once I got into it, I had a hard time putting it down. I had a few minor issues with the plot and a hard time with Lo's character at first ....but she grew on me.<br /><br />Honestly, the suspense was good and I had no idea what was going to happen next but I definitely wanted to find out.<br /><br />All in all this was a creepy (in a good way) and entertaining read, and I look forward to reading more from this author.<br /><br />I would like to thank Goodreads Giveaways for my copy of this book in exchange for an honest review.</span>

  <span id="freeText1494792021248360756" style="display:none">I just knew I was going to love this book because I love the cover. <div id="review_1579795901" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1579795901" />
    <a title="Melissa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9684061-melissa"><img alt="Melissa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528750408p2/9684061.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1579795901?book_show_action=true">Mar 14, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa" href="/user/show/9684061-melissa">Melissa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/29918785-the-woman-in-cabin-10">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9684061-melissa?shelf=suspense-mystery-thriller">suspense-mystery-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9684061-melissa?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9684061-melissa?shelf=dark-and-twisted">dark-and-twisted</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9684061-melissa?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1579795901" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18311666168009829196">If I’m being totally honest, I didn’t go into this book with the highest of expectations. In fact, I’m not even sure what made me request an advanced copy. It’s no secret, I wasn’t a huge fan of <a>In a Dark, Dark Wood</a>. Unlike a lot of other readers, I found it to be kind of slow and predictable. This one on the other hand - <b>it totally worked for me</b>.<br/><br/>A cruise ship in the middle of the ocean turned out to be the perfect setting for a chilling tale. I could feel the ebb and flow of the nausea inducing</span>
  <span id="freeText18311666168009829196" style="display:none">If I’m being totally honest, I didn’t go into this book with the highest of expectations. In fact, I’m not even sure what made me request an advanced copy. It’s no secret, I wasn’t a huge fan of <a>In a Dark, Dark Wood</a>. Unlike a lot of other readers, I found it to be kind of slow and predictable. This one on the other hand - <b>it totally worked for me</b>.<br /><br />A cruise ship in the middle of the ocean turned out to be the perfect setting for a chilling tale. I could feel the ebb and flow of the nausea inducing waves, the panic that set in with the claustrophobic quarters and the fear of being trapped on a ship in the middle of nowhere, with no connection to home. How creepy. <br /><br />Can you imagine your sanity hinging on a tube of Maybelline mascara? I know, it sounds kind of silly, right? That borrowed tube is Lo Blacklock’s only proof that she actually saw a woman in Cabin 10. Does the disappearance of that pink and green tube support Lo’s claim that she saw someone being tossed off the balcony or just confirm that she’s gone completely mad?<br /><br /><i>
  <b>“Sorry, I know this sounds really weird, but I wondered if I could borrow some mascara?”</b>
</i><br /><br />I can tell you the author did a great job of making me question everyone. I was convinced it was all in Lo’s mind. That she was inadvertently making everything up. That she was confused. Until the author managed to throw me off with some of the other shady passengers. Then I felt like maybe I was the one that was confused.<br /><br />I was back and forth so many times with my theories and in the end - I was wrong. <b>I love being wrong</b>. Seriously, is there anything better than reading a suspense/thriller and finding out that you were totally off-base?<br /><br />The beginning was a little bit of a slow start, but it picked up pretty quickly, and next thing you know, I couldn’t put it down. <b>I am so glad, I gave this author another shot.</b> I can’t wait to see what she throws at us next.<br /><br /><i>*ARC provided by Gallery/Scout Press and NetGalley in exchange for an honest review.*</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="18311666168009829196" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1964967973" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1964967973" />
    <a title="Susanne  Strong" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4514828-susanne-strong"><img alt="Susanne  Strong" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583087410p2/4514828.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1964967973?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Susanne  Strong" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Susanne  Strong" href="/user/show/4514828-susanne-strong">Susanne  Strong</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4514828-susanne-strong?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1964967973" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17116454560287543754">4 Stars.<br/>Very Suspenseful!<br/><br/>Lo Blacklock is a travel journalist who is invited to go aboard the Aurora Borealis to do a story on the new ship for her magazine. Lo thinks a week away on a luxury cruise liner sounds like a dream come true. After all, her apartment was just burgled and since she’s been anxious about it, she’s had trouble sleeping ever since. <br/> <br/>As she’s getting ready for her first formal dinner, Lo realizes that she forgot mascara, thus she knocks on the door of Cabin 10 next door to bo</span>
  <span id="freeText17116454560287543754" style="display:none">4 Stars.<br />Very Suspenseful!<br /><br />Lo Blacklock is a travel journalist who is invited to go aboard the Aurora Borealis to do a story on the new ship for her magazine. Lo thinks a week away on a luxury cruise liner sounds like a dream come true. After all, her apartment was just burgled and since she’s been anxious about it, she’s had trouble sleeping ever since. <br /> <br />As she’s getting ready for her first formal dinner, Lo realizes that she forgot mascara, thus she knocks on the door of Cabin 10 next door to borrow a tube of Maybelline Mascara from a beautiful young woman. (Honestly, this got me thinking, who would do this? Would you? I sure wouldn't (simply because of the germ factor, but whatever!) Anyhow, I digress..) During the cocktail hour and dinner, Lo gets sloshed. Her work assignment is the last thing on her mind. <br /><br />That night, she has trouble sleeping and Lo is certain that someone was tossed off of the balcony from Cabin 10. Lo reports it to security. None of the passengers or staff are unaccounted for. Was she so drunk that she imagined it? Has she gone mad? No one believes her. Yet she is sure that something bad happened.<br /><br />As the suspense builds, we the readers feel the tension build in the pits of our stomach, wondering, is Lo crazy? If she isn’t, how come no one can corroborate her story? What is going on? <br /><br />Ruth Ware did a great job in keeping me on the edge of my seat. I couldn’t wait to find out what the deal was. I will admit that a few things about the book really bothered me … (hence the reason for the 4 v. 5 star rating). Specifically: Lo’s assignment and her lack of concern about actually doing it, and her relationship with Judah, which I never felt strongly about. I have read Ruth Ware’s other novel (In a Dark Dark Wood) and enjoyed this one much more. I listened to the audiobook version of this and thought the narrator did a great job.<br /><br />Published on Goodreads and Amazon on 4/8/17.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17116454560287543754" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1855459046" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1855459046" />
    <a title="Matthew" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16254355-matthew"><img alt="Matthew" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464987365p2/16254355.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1855459046?book_show_action=true">Apr 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matthew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matthew" href="/user/show/16254355-matthew">Matthew</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9781509413836" href="/book/show/30455212-the-woman-in-cabin-10">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=gr_awards_2016">gr_awards_2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=2017">2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1855459046" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer38673704811844011">As soon as I started reading this and posting statuses, I got several replies about how much people did not like this book. I cannot remember getting that much negative feedback about a book on my progress statuses. So, I figured I would either be joining the world in slamming this book, or I would be trying to make my case about how everyone was wrong.<br/><br/>Well, I am kinda in the middle.<br/><br/>I didn’t hate the book, but it didn’t blow me away. It feels like it was intentionally written to fit in with the </span>
  <span id="freeText38673704811844011" style="display:none">As soon as I started reading this and posting statuses, I got several replies about how much people did not like this book. I cannot remember getting that much negative feedback about a book on my progress statuses. So, I figured I would either be joining the world in slamming this book, or I would be trying to make my case about how everyone was wrong.<br /><br />Well, I am kinda in the middle.<br /><br />I didn’t hate the book, but it didn’t blow me away. It feels like it was intentionally written to fit in with the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19288043.Gone_Girl" title="Gone Girl by Gillian Flynn" rel="nofollow noopener">Gone Girl</a>/<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22557272.The_Girl_on_the_Train" title="The Girl on the Train by Paula Hawkins" rel="nofollow noopener">The Girl on the Train</a> genre. The biggest difference is that I wouldn’t say that any of the characters were really hateable. Maybe a few that could be slightly disliked, but nothing like the aforementioned books.<br /><br />The plot was a little silly, but I was willing to suspend my disbelief for the sake of a quick read. At times I was really into what was going on, at other times I was like “okay, enough of that, let’s move on”. I do think that the general idea of how a mystery-on-a-boat was presented did feel unique and there were a few surprises that caught me off guard.<br /><br />Do I recommend: Did you like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19288043.Gone_Girl" title="Gone Girl by Gillian Flynn" rel="nofollow noopener">Gone Girl</a>/<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22557272.The_Girl_on_the_Train" title="The Girl on the Train by Paula Hawkins" rel="nofollow noopener">The Girl on the Train</a>? You might like this (FYI – I hated Girl On The Train, but thought Gone Girl was okay).<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="38673704811844011" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2209213062?book_show_action=true">Dec 09, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma Giordano" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma Giordano" href="/user/show/30604861-emma-giordano">Emma Giordano</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2209213062" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4260351075015102700">I can't decide between 3.5 stars and 4 stars, but I enjoyed this read! I struggled with it a bit, but I enjoyed the ending overall.<br/><br/>TW: home invasion, anxiety (panic attacks), substance abuse, lowkey sexual assault<br/><br/>I feel as if this is one of those books that I don't have much to say on. I wasn't the biggest fan of the writing and the beginning was slightly boring, but the ending of the story was thrilling and very clever in my opinion. <br/><br/>I was surprised to find a very positive portray of medication</span>
  <span id="freeText4260351075015102700" style="display:none">I can't decide between 3.5 stars and 4 stars, but I enjoyed this read! I struggled with it a bit, but I enjoyed the ending overall.<br /><br />TW: home invasion, anxiety (panic attacks), substance abuse, lowkey sexual assault<br /><br />I feel as if this is one of those books that I don't have much to say on. I wasn't the biggest fan of the writing and the beginning was slightly boring, but the ending of the story was thrilling and very clever in my opinion. <br /><br />I was surprised to find a very positive portray of medication to treat mental illness. Lo takes antidepressants for her anxiety and treats them as an essential part of her functioning. She suffers from a lot of stigma as a result of her medication, but she continues to be confident in her decisions related treatment and that really pleased me.<br /><br />There is a non-consensual groping scene that was swept under the rug, which made me very uncomfortable. I guess it's ignored because they are past lovers or they were both drunk but for whatever reason, I found this scene very troubling. Non-consensual touching should never be dismissed so easily.<br /><br />Overall, a mostly enjoyable read. The ending is twisted and well though out enough to make up for a not so great beginning, in my opinion.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4260351075015102700" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer10913513036343266188">Lo Blacklock, a journalist who works for a travel magazine, is given an assignment to go aboard the small but stunning luxury cruise ship "The Aurora" for a week. But one night Lo is woken by a noise and she thinks the woman in the next cabin (Cabin 10) was thrown overboard. When she tells the fellow passengers and crew they don't really believe her. According to their records no one was staying in the cabin next to Lo's. What really happened to the woman who was in the next cabin? Lo does some </span>
  <span id="freeText10913513036343266188" style="display:none">Lo Blacklock, a journalist who works for a travel magazine, is given an assignment to go aboard the small but stunning luxury cruise ship "The Aurora" for a week. But one night Lo is woken by a noise and she thinks the woman in the next cabin (Cabin 10) was thrown overboard. When she tells the fellow passengers and crew they don't really believe her. According to their records no one was staying in the cabin next to Lo's. What really happened to the woman who was in the next cabin? Lo does some investigating to find out. Along the way she starts receiving threats to "stop digging". Who can she trust? Did she just imagine all this?<br /><br />This was an enjoyable suspense story. I really liked the setting on the lavish cruise ship and its voyage in the North Sea with its bad/no internet connection making Lo seem cut off from the rest of the world on a small and sometimes claustrophobic ship with maybe a murderer on board. I found the characters interesting and I was curious to find out what had happened to the woman in cabin 10.<br /><br />Another good mystery by Ruth Ware.<br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_1697834069" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1697834069" />
    <a title="Sam Quixote" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5759543-sam-quixote"><img alt="Sam Quixote" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529183438p2/5759543.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1697834069?book_show_action=true">Jul 14, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sam Quixote" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sam Quixote" href="/user/show/5759543-sam-quixote">Sam Quixote</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781846558900" href="/book/show/26889456-the-woman-in-cabin-10">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1697834069" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12088013599824867669">Laura Blacklock is a travel journalist given a career-boosting opportunity to cover the maiden voyage of a luxury cruise liner headed to see the Northern Lights. On her first night there she meets a mysterious woman in the cabin next to hers, cabin 10, and then later hears a scream and the sounds of a body being dumped into the sea, seeing what she thinks is blood on the neighbouring railing. Except the cabin is empty and no-one on the ship matches the woman’s description. A heavy drinker and us</span>
  <span id="freeText12088013599824867669" style="display:none">Laura Blacklock is a travel journalist given a career-boosting opportunity to cover the maiden voyage of a luxury cruise liner headed to see the Northern Lights. On her first night there she meets a mysterious woman in the cabin next to hers, cabin 10, and then later hears a scream and the sounds of a body being dumped into the sea, seeing what she thinks is blood on the neighbouring railing. Except the cabin is empty and no-one on the ship matches the woman’s description. A heavy drinker and using prescription pills for anxiety and depression, as well as dealing with the trauma of a recent home-invasion, is Laura imagining things – or is there a murderer on board? <br /><br />I really enjoyed Ruth Ware’s debut novel In a Dark, Dark Wood, so I was excited to read her latest, The Woman in Cabin 10; unfortunately it’s a disappointing let-down and quite a boring read. <br /><br />My biggest problem is with how quickly exciting events are dealt with and how looooong the dreary aftermath is dwelt on. For example, the book opens with Laura being burgled while also being in her London flat: exciting. Then there’s page after page after page of seeing her shaken up, having trouble sleeping, drinking, worrying, traumatised: dull. Dull, static, ordinary, and predictable to read but we still have to plod through the pages while Ware underlines to the reader that Laura is unnerved. Duh. <br /><br />Then we get on the boat, and, following too many pages of Laura schmoozing with vapid guests, we get to the murder in the night: exciting. And then we have to endure page after page of Laura explaining what she’s seen (and what the reader has also just seen) to the ship’s security officer in detail – it’s so repetitive! How about throwing in a line like “I explained what I had seen to the ship’s security officer but he didn’t believe me, even insinuating doubt by mentioning the booze I’d had that night and looking toward the pills by the sink” to skip over it all?<br /><br />Then we have to sit through page after page of Laura and the security officer meeting the staff to see if the woman in cabin 10 isn’t one of them – even though the reader knows it’s not going to be that easy and nothing interesting happens during the interviews to make doing so worthwhile anyway. A simple line like “I spent the morning meeting the staff but the woman in cabin 10 wasn’t among them” could’ve been dropped in and we could move on! But I guess Ware had to meet a certain page count. <br /><br />Ware is then content to tread water while Laura continues to question herself, wondering who she can trust, (ie. doing nothing) with the occasional cheap cornball thrill scare tossed in – for example, the writing on the steamed-up mirror. Reading this increasingly threadbare story as it painfully progresses is like wading through sludge! What little tension there is all but disappears once the reader finds out what’s going on but still we’ve got to go through the motions of Laura escaping, etc. to get to the end some 70-ish pages later. Awful stuff. <br /><br />It doesn’t help that Laura isn’t an engaging protagonist at all. What the book really needed was a compelling Poirot-type who could wring the drama and tension out of the situation. But no, we got plain, dull old Laura bumbling about uselessly instead. <br /><br />I can see Ruth Ware aiming for a cross between Agatha Christie and Patricia Highsmith with this novel but she falls far short of both and instead creates a slow-moving and far from thrilling novel with a stereotypical murderer/motive as the reader’s unsatisfying reward. The setup has potential but Ware fails to realise it – The Woman in Cabin 10 is an immensely tedious chore to slog through.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12088013599824867669" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2951118610" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2951118610" />
    <a title="RedemptionDenied" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/55677020-redemptiondenied"><img alt="RedemptionDenied" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2951118610?book_show_action=true">Aug 25, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="RedemptionDenied" class="user" itemprop="url" name="RedemptionDenied" href="/user/show/55677020-redemptiondenied">RedemptionDenied</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55677020-redemptiondenied?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55677020-redemptiondenied?shelf=i-didn-t-see-that-coming">i-didn-t-see-that-coming</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55677020-redemptiondenied?shelf=2019">2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55677020-redemptiondenied?shelf=suspense">suspense</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2951118610" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13371154682944974029">I started this - weeks ago, and finally got back to it - in the early hours of Sunday morning. I like Blacklock (main character) - she's funny. Or am I reading it wrong? Whatever. I never did guess as to what was going on. I flirted with theories all-over-the-place and I wasn't even close. I thought I had it sussed, at one point - but nope. Not even close, as much as I hate to admit it. <br/><br/>A travel writer gets the opportunity to join other journalists, photographers and influential people on the ma</span>
  <span id="freeText13371154682944974029" style="display:none">I started this - weeks ago, and finally got back to it - in the early hours of Sunday morning. I like Blacklock (main character) - she's funny. Or am I reading it wrong? Whatever. I never did guess as to what was going on. I flirted with theories all-over-the-place and I wasn't even close. I thought I had it sussed, at one point - but nope. Not even close, as much as I hate to admit it. <br /><br />A travel writer gets the opportunity to join other journalists, photographers and influential people on the maiden voyage of a luxury-cruise ship, which is basically a large yacht, and owned by businessman, Richard Bullmer. Her boss, Rowan, was supposed to be going on the five-day itinerary, but due to unforeseen circumstances, Laura (Lo) Blacklock (she amused me) - gets the gig. Lucky. <br /><br />After spending the first evening, meeting the other guests (some she was already acquainted with) - joining in the festivities, drinking, dining, drinking, conversing and drinking some more - she decides to call it a night and goes back to her designated cabin. Cabin 9. Which is the Linnaeus suite. Linnaeus, Carolus was a Swedish botanist (1707-78) - founder of modern systematic botany and zoology. Yeah. I looked it up. Cabin 10 is the Palmgren suite.<br /><br />After falling asleep, she wakes with a start, in the early hours, thinking she may've heard someone scream. Unable to get back to la-la-land, she picks up her book from the bedside table, turns the page and hears something else: the veranda door of the cabin next-door (cabin 10) opening, then a big splash. Huh? What was that noise? Was it a body hitting the water? She goes to investigate (nose) and sees blood-smear on the veranda door to cabin 10. She reports her findings to the head of security, and so begins her tumble down the rabbit hole. <br /><br />So, who was the girl in the cabin next to Blacklocks? The girl who gave her the mascara, the only tangible evidence that Lo has that there was someone in cabin 10. It's a mystery. Did she imagine the girl? She drank enough in the evening, to see the "Pink Elephants On Parade."<br /><br />In conclusion: I enjoyed this more than I thought I would - so that's a bonus. As the story is told from a first-person perspective (Lo's) - it's difficult to guess what's going on. I didn't know, until Blacklock figured stuff out, and even then I wasn't too sure, as she's an unreliable narrator.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13371154682944974029" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
